**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Implementation

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement RBAC authorization. Identify: the RBACAuthorizer with its Authorize method (in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/), the SubjectAccessEvaluator, the DefaultRuleResolver that resolves PolicyRules for a user, the SubjectAccessReview REST handler, the bootstrap RBAC policy definitions, and the policy-based storage for Role and ClusterRoleBinding objects with escalation prevention.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes RBAC authorization implementation. Here's a summary of what I found:

## RBAC Authorization Implementation Summary

I've identified and documented **25+ key Go source files** and **40+ important symbols** implementing RBAC in Kubernetes:

### **Core Components:**

1. **RBACAuthorizer** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`) - Main authorization engine that checks requests against policies using a visitor pattern and rule mapping

2. **DefaultRuleResolver** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`) - Resolves all applicable PolicyRules for a user by visiting ClusterRoleBindings and RoleBindings, with methods for RulesFor, VisitRulesFor, and GetRoleReferenceRules

3. **SubjectAccessEvaluator** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go`) - Evaluates which subjects have permissions to perform actions by traversing role bindings

4. **SubjectAccessReview REST Handler** (`pkg/registry/authorization/subjectaccessreview/rest.go`) - Stateless REST endpoint that evaluates authorization queries and returns allow/deny decisions

### **Bootstrap Policies:**

- `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/policy.go` - ClusterRoles, NodeRules
- `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/namespace_policy.go` - Namespace-scoped defaults
- `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/controller_policy.go` - Controller permissions

### **Escalation Prevention:**

- `pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go` - Functions for EscalationAllowed, RoleEscalationAuthorized, and BindingAuthorized checks
- Four **Policy-Based Storage** implementations that wrap and intercept Create/Update operations for Roles, RoleBindings, ClusterRoles, and ClusterRoleBindings to prevent privilege escalation

Authorization Implementation Overview\\n\\nThe RBAC (Role-Based Access Control) authorization system in Kubernetes is implemented across multiple packages and files, orchestrating a sophisticated hierarchy of role resolution, policy enforcement, and escalation prevention. Here's a comprehensive breakdown of the key components:\\n\\n## Core Authorization Engine\\n\\nThe RBACAuthorizer (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go:50) is the primary authorizer that implements the authorizer.Authorizer interface. Its Authorize method (line 75) evaluates requests against policies by delegating to a RequestToRuleMapper (line 37), which provides the interface for retrieving PolicyRules that apply to users. The authorizer uses an authorizingVisitor pattern to check rules and short-circuit on first allow.\\n\\n## Rule Resolution Hierarchy\\n\\nThe DefaultRuleResolver (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:91) is the concrete implementation of AuthorizationRuleResolver (line 37) that resolves all PolicyRules applicable to a user in a namespace. It implements:\\n- RulesFor (line 118): Returns accumulated PolicyRules for a user\\n- VisitRulesFor (line 179): Visits rules for a user across ClusterRoleBindings and RoleBindings\\n- GetRoleReferenceRules (line 240): Resolves Role/ClusterRole references from role bindings\\n\\nThe resolver depends on four getter/lister interfaces:\\n- RoleGetter (line 102): Fetches Role objects\\n- RoleBindingLister (line 106): Lists RoleBindings in a namespace\\n- ClusterRoleGetter (line 110): Fetches ClusterRole objects  \\n- ClusterRoleBindingLister (line 114): Lists ClusterRoleBindings cluster-wide\\n\\nIn practice, these are implemented by adapter types in rbac.go (lines 195-225) that wrap informer listers.\\n\\n## Subject Access Evaluation\\n\\nThe SubjectAccessEvaluator (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go:42) implements SubjectLocator and provides the AllowedSubjects method (line 64) that returns which subjects (users, groups, service accounts) have permissions to perform an action. It traverses both cluster-wide and namespace-scoped role bindings, matching rules against the provided request attributes.\\n\\n## Subject Access Review REST Handler\\n\\nThe REST handler (pkg/registry/authorization/subjectaccessreview/rest.go:35) implements a StatelessCreateRest that handles SubjectAccessReview API requests. Its Create method (line 63) validates the request and uses the authorizer to evaluate the decision, then returns a SubjectAccessReviewStatus with allowed/denied/reason fields.\\n\\n## Bootstrap RBAC Policies\\n\\nBootstrap policies are defined in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/ with three main modules:\\n\\n1. policy.go: Defines ClusterRoles() (line 197) and ClusterRoleBindings() that provide core system permissions for components like system:kube-scheduler, system:kube-controller-manager. Also includes NodeRules() (line 112) for kubelet permissions.\\n\\n2. namespace_policy.go: Provides NamespaceRoles() and NamespaceRoleBindings() for namespace-scoped default roles in system namespaces (kube-system, kube-public, etc.).\\n\\n3. controller_policy.go: Defines ControllerRoles() and ControllerRoleBindings() for various controller service accounts (replication-controller, horizontal-pod-autoscaler, etc.).\\n\\nThese policies are reconciled at startup via PostStartHook in pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go (line 131).\\n\\n## Escalation Prevention\\n\\nThe escalation prevention system is implemented through multiple mechanisms:\\n\\n1. escalation_check.go provides three key functions:\\n   - EscalationAllowed (line 32): Checks if user is in system:masters group\\n   - RoleEscalationAuthorized (line 55): Checks if user has \\\"escalate\\\" verb on role/clusterrole resources\\n   - BindingAuthorized (line 101): Checks if user has \\\"bind\\\" verb on the specific role being referenced\\n\\n2. Validation via ConfirmNoEscalation (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:53) checks that a user attempting to create/update a role/binding doesn't grant permissions they don't already have.\\n\\n## Policy-Based Storage Implementation\\n\\nThe four policy-based storage implementations wrap the standard storage and enforce escalation prevention at the storage layer:\\n\\n1. pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go: For Role objects\\n2. pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go: For RoleBinding objects\\n3. pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go: For ClusterRole objects (with special handling for aggregationRule requiring cluster-admin)\\n4. pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go: For ClusterRoleBinding objects\\n\\nEach Storage type wraps rest.StandardStorage and intercepts Create and Update operations. They check escalation permissions before delegating to the underlying storage, using either:\\n- EscalationAllowed() for system:masters bypass\\n- RoleEscalationAuthorized() for explicit escalate permission\\n- BindingAuthorized() for role binding-specific checks\\n- ConfirmNoEscalation() to verify the user already possesses the permissions being granted\\n\\n## Integration Points\\n\\nThe RESTStorageProvider (pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go:61) orchestrates the entire storage setup:\\n1. Creates base storage instances for roles, rolebindings, clusterroles, clusterrolebindings\\n2. Wraps them with policy-based storage implementations\\n3. Creates a DefaultRuleResolver for escalation validation\\n4. Registers the PostStartHook for bootstrap policy reconciliation\\n\\nThe authorizer configuration (pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go:123) instantiates the RBACAuthorizer with RoleGetter/RoleBindingLister/ClusterRoleGetter/ClusterRoleBindingLister adapters that fetch data from informers, enabling real-time authorization decisions based on current cluster state.\"\n}\n",

Here's a comprehensive breakdown of the key components:\\n\\n## Core Authorization Engine\\n\\nThe RBACAuthorizer (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go:50) is the primary authorizer that implements the authorizer.Authorizer interface. Its Authorize method (line 75) evaluates requests against policies by delegating to a RequestToRuleMapper (line 37), which provides the interface for retrieving PolicyRules that apply to users. The authorizer uses an authorizingVisitor pattern to check rules and short-circuit on first allow.\\n\\n## Rule Resolution Hierarchy\\n\\nThe DefaultRuleResolver (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:91) is the concrete implementation of AuthorizationRuleResolver (line 37) that resolves all PolicyRules applicable to a user in a namespace. It implements:\\n- RulesFor (line 118): Returns accumulated PolicyRules for a user\\n- VisitRulesFor (line 179): Visits rules for a user across ClusterRoleBindings and RoleBindings\\n- GetRoleReferenceRules (line 240): Resolves Role/ClusterRole references from role bindings\\n\\nThe resolver depends on four getter/lister interfaces:\\n- RoleGetter (line 102): Fetches Role objects\\n- RoleBindingLister (line 106): Lists RoleBindings in a namespace\\n- ClusterRoleGetter (line 110): Fetches ClusterRole objects  \\n- ClusterRoleBindingLister (line 114): Lists ClusterRoleBindings cluster-wide\\n\\nIn practice, these are implemented by adapter types in rbac.go (lines 195-225) that wrap informer listers.\\n\\n## Subject Access Evaluation\\n\\nThe SubjectAccessEvaluator (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go:42) implements SubjectLocator and provides the AllowedSubjects method (line 64) that returns which subjects (users, groups, service accounts) have permissions to perform an action. It traverses both cluster-wide and namespace-scoped role bindings, matching rules against the provided request attributes.\\n\\n## Subject Access Review REST Handler\\n\\nThe REST handler (pkg/registry/authorization/subjectaccessreview/rest.go:35) implements a StatelessCreateRest that handles SubjectAccessReview API requests. Its Create method (line 63) validates the request and uses the authorizer to evaluate the decision, then returns a SubjectAccessReviewStatus with allowed/denied/reason fields.\\n\\n## Bootstrap RBAC Policies\\n\\nBootstrap policies are defined in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/ with three main modules:\\n\\n1. policy.go: Defines ClusterRoles() (line 197) and ClusterRoleBindings() that provide core system permissions for components like system:kube-scheduler, system:kube-controller-manager. Also includes NodeRules() (line 112) for kubelet permissions.\\n\\n2. namespace_policy.go: Provides NamespaceRoles() and NamespaceRoleBindings() for namespace-scoped default roles in system namespaces (kube-system, kube-public, etc.).\\n\\n3. controller_policy.go: Defines ControllerRoles() and ControllerRoleBindings() for various controller service accounts (replication-controller, horizontal-pod-autoscaler, etc.).\\n\\nThese policies are reconciled at startup via PostStartHook in pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go (line 131).\\n\\n## Escalation Prevention\\n\\nThe escalation prevention system is implemented through multiple mechanisms:\\n\\n1. escalation_check.go provides three key functions:\\n   - EscalationAllowed (line 32): Checks if user is in system:masters group\\n   - RoleEscalationAuthorized (line 55): Checks if user has \\\"escalate\\\" verb on role/clusterrole resources\\n   - BindingAuthorized (line 101): Checks if user has \\\"bind\\\" verb on the specific role being referenced\\n\\n2. Validation via ConfirmNoEscalation (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:53) checks that a user attempting to create/update a role/binding doesn't grant permissions they don't already have.\\n\\n## Policy-Based Storage Implementation\\n\\nThe four policy-based storage implementations wrap the standard storage and enforce escalation prevention at the storage layer:\\n\\n1. pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go: For Role objects\\n2. pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go: For RoleBinding objects\\n3. pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go: For ClusterRole objects (with special handling for aggregationRule requiring cluster-admin)\\n4. pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go: For ClusterRoleBinding objects\\n\\nEach Storage type wraps rest.StandardStorage and intercepts Create and Update operations. They check escalation permissions before delegating to the underlying storage, using either:\\n- EscalationAllowed() for system:masters bypass\\n- RoleEscalationAuthorized() for explicit escalate permission\\n- BindingAuthorized() for role binding-specific checks\\n- ConfirmNoEscalation() to verify the user already possesses the permissions being granted\\n\\n## Integration Points\\n\\nThe RESTStorageProvider (pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go:61) orchestrates the entire storage setup:\\n1.
